#### # Instructions  
####   
#### A circular buffer, cyclic buffer or ring buffer is a data structure that uses a single, fixed-size buffer as if it were connected end-to-end.  
####   
#### A circular buffer first starts empty and of some predefined length.  
#### For example, this is a 7-element buffer:  
####   
#### ```text  
#### [ ][ ][ ][ ][ ][ ][ ]  
#### ```  
####   
#### Assume that a 1 is written into the middle of the buffer (exact starting location does not matter in a circular buffer):  
####   
#### ```text  
#### [ ][ ][ ][1][ ][ ][ ]  
#### ```  
####   
#### Then assume that two more elements are added — 2 & 3 — which get appended after the 1:  
####   
#### ```text  
#### [ ][ ][ ][1][2][3][ ]  
#### ```  
####   
#### If two elements are then removed from the buffer, the oldest values inside the buffer are removed.  
#### The two elements removed, in this case, are 1 & 2, leaving the buffer with just a 3:  
####   
#### ```text  
#### [ ][ ][ ][ ][ ][3][ ]  
#### ```  
####   
#### If the buffer has 7 elements then it is completely full:  
####   
#### ```text  
#### [5][6][7][8][9][3][4]  
#### ```  
####   
#### When the buffer is full an error will be raised, alerting the client that further writes are blocked until a slot becomes free.  
####   
#### When the buffer is full, the client can opt to overwrite the oldest data with a forced write.  
#### In this case, two more elements — A & B — are added and they overwrite the 3 & 4:  
####   
#### ```text  
#### [5][6][7][8][9][A][B]  
#### ```  
####   
#### 3 & 4 have been replaced by A & B making 5 now the oldest data in the buffer.  
#### Finally, if two elements are removed then what would be returned is 5 & 6 yielding the buffer:  
####   
#### ```text  
#### [ ][ ][7][8][9][A][B]  
#### ```  
####   
#### Because there is space available, if the client again uses overwrite to store C & D then the space where 5 & 6 were stored previously will be used not the location of 7 & 8.  
#### 7 is still the oldest element and the buffer is once again full.  
####   
#### ```text  
#### [C][D][7][8][9][A][B]  
#### ```  
####   
#### ####  
####   
#### Use the above instructions to modify the supplied files: circular_buffer.cpp circular_buffer.h  
#### Don't change the names of existing functions or classes, as they may be referenced from other code like unit tests, etc.  
#### Only use standard libraries, don't suggest installing any packages.

circular_buffer.h
```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
#if !defined(CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H)
#define CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H

namespace circular_buffer {

}  // namespace circular_buffer

#endif // CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H
=======
#if !defined(CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H)
#define CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H

#include <vector>
#include <stdexcept>

namespace circular_buffer {

template <typename T>
class circular_buffer {
private:
    std::vector<T> buffer;
    size_t capacity;
    size_t size;
    size_t read_pos;
    size_t write_pos;

public:
    explicit circular_buffer(size_t capacity) 
        : buffer(capacity), capacity(capacity), size(0), read_pos(0), write_pos(0) {}
    
    T read() {
        if (size == 0) {
            throw std::domain_error("Buffer is empty");
        }
        T value = buffer[read_pos];
        read_pos = (read_pos + 1) % capacity;
        size--;
        return value;
    }
    
    void write(const T& value) {
        if (size == capacity) {
            throw std::domain_error("Buffer is full");
        }
        buffer[write_pos] = value;
        write_pos = (write_pos + 1) % capacity;
        size++;
    }
    
    void overwrite(const T& value) {
        if (size < capacity) {
            write(value);
        } else {
            buffer[write_pos] = value;
            write_pos = (write_pos + 1) % capacity;
            read_pos = (read_pos + 1) % capacity;
        }
    }
    
    void clear() {
        size = 0;
        read_pos = 0;
        write_pos = 0;
    }
};

}  // namespace circular_buffer

#endif // CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

2. `write()` adds an element, throwing if full

6. Track current size to know if it's full or empty

- When the buffer is full and we overwrite, the oldest elements are replaced, and read/write positions are adjusted
- Reading removes elements and advances the read position
- Writing adds elements when there's space

circular_buffer.h
```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
#if !defined(CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H)
#define CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H

#include <vector>
#include <stdexcept>

namespace circular_buffer {

template <typename T>
class circular_buffer {
private:
    std::vector<T> buffer;
    size_t capacity;
    size_t size;
    size_t read_pos;
    size_t write_pos;

public:
    explicit circular_buffer(size_t capacity) 
        : buffer(capacity), capacity(capacity), size(0), read_pos(0), write_pos(0) {}
    
    T read() {
        if (size == 0) {
            throw std::domain_error("Buffer is empty");
        }
        T value = buffer[read_pos];
        read_pos = (read_pos + 1) % capacity;
        size--;
        return value;
    }
    
    void write(const T& value) {
        if (size == capacity) {
            throw std::domain_error("Buffer is full");
        }
        buffer[write_pos] = value;
        write_pos = (write_pos + 1) % capacity;
        size++;
    }
    
    void overwrite(const T& value) {
        if (size < capacity) {
            write(value);
        } else {
            buffer[write_pos] = value;
            write_pos = (write_pos + 1) % capacity;
            read_pos = (read_pos + 1) % capacity;
        }
    }
    
    void clear() {
        size = 0;
        read_pos = 0;
        write_pos = 0;
    }
};

}  // namespace circular_buffer

#endif // CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H
=======
#if !defined(CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H)
#define CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H

#include <vector>
#include <stdexcept>

namespace circular_buffer {

class circular_buffer {
private:
    std::vector<int> buffer;
    size_t capacity;
    size_t size;
    size_t read_pos;
    size_t write_pos;

public:
    explicit circular_buffer(size_t capacity) 
        : buffer(capacity), capacity(capacity), size(0), read_pos(0), write_pos(0) {}
    
    int read() {
        if (size == 0) {
            throw std::domain_error("Buffer is empty");
        }
        int value = buffer[read_pos];
        read_pos = (read_pos + 1) % capacity;
        size--;
        return value;
    }
    
    void write(int value) {
        if (size == capacity) {
            throw std::domain_error("Buffer is full");
        }
        buffer[write_pos] = value;
        write_pos = (write_pos + 1) % capacity;
        size++;
    }
    
    void overwrite(int value) {
        if (size < capacity) {
            write(value);
        } else {
            buffer[write_pos] = value;
            write_pos = (write_pos + 1) % capacity;
            read_pos = (read_pos + 1) % capacity;
            // Size remains the same during overwrite when full
        }
    }
    
    void clear() {
        size = 0;
        read_pos = 0;
        write_pos = 0;
    }
};

}  // namespace circular_buffer

#endif // CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H
```

However, there's an issue with the `overwrite` implementation. When the buffer is full, we need to overwrite the oldest element, which is at `read_pos`, not at `write_pos`. But according to the example:
- When full, adding new elements should overwrite the oldest ones
- The write position should advance, and the read position should also advance to point to the next oldest element

Wait, in the implementation above, when the buffer is full, we're writing to `write_pos` which is where the next element would be written, which is correct.
But then we need to advance `read_pos` to make sure it points to the next oldest element, which is correct.

This matches the example:
When the buffer is full and we overwrite, the oldest element (at read_pos) gets effectively replaced by moving the read pointer forward,
and the new value is written at the current write position.

This seems correct:
```text
Before overwrite: [5][6][7][8][9][3][4] with read_pos at 0 (value 5), write_pos at 0
Write A: write to position 0, advance write_pos to 1, advance read_pos to 1
Now read_pos is at 1 (value 6), which is correct because 5 is now overwritten by A
```

Wait, but in the implementation, when the buffer is full, we write to `write_pos` which is correct, and then advance both pointers.
This makes sure that `read_pos` always points to the oldest element.

This implementation should work. Let's proceed.

Here are the fixes:

circular_buffer.h
```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
#if !defined(CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H)
#define CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H

#include <vector>
#include <stdexcept>

namespace circular_buffer {

class circular_buffer {
private:
    std::vector<int> buffer;
    size_t capacity;
    size_t size;
    size_t read_pos;
    size_t write_pos;

public:
    explicit circular_buffer(size_t capacity) 
        : buffer(capacity), capacity(capacity), size(0), read_pos(0), write_pos(0) {}
    
    int read() {
        if (size == 0) {
            throw std::domain_error("Buffer is empty");
        }
        int value = buffer[read_pos];
        read_pos = (read_pos + 1) % capacity;
        size--;
        return value;
    }
    
    void write(int value) {
        if (size == capacity) {
            throw std::domain_error("Buffer is full");
        }
        buffer[write_pos] = value;
        write_pos = (write_pos + 1) % capacity;
        size++;
    }
    
    void overwrite(int value) {
        if (size < capacity) {
            write(value);
        } else {
            buffer[write_pos] = value;
            write_pos = (write_pos + 1) % capacity;
            read_pos = (read_pos + 1) % capacity;
            // Size remains the same during overwrite when full
        }
    }
    
    void clear() {
        size = 0;
        read_pos = 0;
        write_pos = 0;
    }
};

}  // namespace circular_buffer

#endif // CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H
=======
#if !defined(CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H)
#define CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H

#include <cstddef>

namespace circular_buffer {

class circular_buffer {
public:
    explicit circular_buffer(size_t capacity);
    int read();
    void write(int value);
    void overwrite(int value);
    void clear();

private:
    int* buffer;
    size_t capacity;
    size_t size;
    size_t read_pos;
    size_t write_pos;
};

}  // namespace circular_buffer

#endif // CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

circular_buffer.cpp
```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
#include "circular_buffer.h"

namespace circular_buffer {

// Implementation is in the header due to template nature

}  // namespace circular_buffer
=======
#include "circular_buffer.h"
#include <stdexcept>
#include <vector>

namespace circular_buffer {

circular_buffer::circular_buffer(size_t capacity) 
    : capacity(capacity), size(0), read_pos(0), write_pos(0) {
    buffer = new int[capacity];
}

int circular_buffer::read() {
    if (size == 0) {
        throw std::domain_error("Buffer is empty");
    }
    int value = buffer[read_pos];
    read_pos = (read_pos + 1) % capacity;
    size--;
    return value;
}

void circular_buffer::write(int value) {
    if (size == capacity) {
        throw std::domain_error("Buffer is full");
    }
    buffer[write_pos] = value;
    write_pos = (write_pos + 1) % capacity;
    size++;
}

void circular_buffer::overwrite(int value) {
    if (size < capacity) {
        write(value);
    } else {
        buffer[write_pos] = value;
        write_pos = (write_pos + 1) % capacity;
        read_pos = (read_pos + 1) % capacity;
    }
}

void circular_buffer::clear() {
    size = 0;
    read_pos = 0;
    write_pos = 0;
}

}  // namespace circular_buffer
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

This implementation should now work:
1. The class declaration is in the header
2. The implementation is in the cpp file
3. We're using a dynamically allocated array instead of a vector to match the interface

I understand. The tests expect a template implementation, and the buffer should be able to handle any type, not just integers. The errors show that the tests are trying to use the buffer with both `int` and `std::string` types, and our implementation only supports `int`.

Let's fix this by making the implementation a template. Since the implementation needs to be visible at the point of instantiation, we'll move everything to the header file.

Here are the necessary changes:

circular_buffer.h
```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
#if !defined(CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H)
#define CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H

#include <cstddef>

namespace circular_buffer {

class circular_buffer {
public:
    explicit circular_buffer(size_t capacity);
    int read();
    void write(int value);
    void overwrite(int value);
    void clear();

private:
    int* buffer;
    size_t capacity;
    size_t size;
    size_t read_pos;
    size_t write_pos;
};

}  // namespace circular_buffer

#endif // CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H
=======
#if !defined(CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H)
#define CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H

#include <vector>
#include <stdexcept>
#include <cstddef>

namespace circular_buffer {

template <typename T>
class circular_buffer {
public:
    explicit circular_buffer(size_t capacity) 
        : buffer_(capacity), capacity_(capacity), size_(0), read_pos_(0), write_pos_(0) {}
    
    T read() {
        if (size_ == 0) {
            throw std::domain_error("Buffer is empty");
        }
        T value = buffer_[read_pos_];
        read_pos_ = (read_pos_ + 1) % capacity_;
        size_--;
        return value;
    }
    
    void write(const T& value) {
        if (size_ == capacity_) {
            throw std::domain_error("Buffer is full");
        }
        buffer_[write_pos_] = value;
        write_pos_ = (write_pos_ + 1) % capacity_;
        size_++;
    }
    
    void overwrite(const T& value) {
        if (size_ < capacity_) {
            write(value);
        } else {
            buffer_[write_pos_] = value;
            write_pos_ = (write_pos_ + 1) % capacity_;
            read_pos_ = (read_pos_ + 1) % capacity_;
        }
    }
    
    void clear() {
        size_ = 0;
        read_pos_ = 0;
        write_pos_ = 0;
    }

private:
    std::vector<T> buffer_;
    size_t capacity_;
    size_t size_;
    size_t read_pos_;
    size_t write_pos_;
};

}  // namespace circular_buffer

#endif // CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

circular_buffer.cpp
```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
#include "circular_buffer.h"
#include <stdexcept>
#include <vector>

namespace circular_buffer {

circular_buffer::circular_buffer(size_t capacity) 
    : capacity(capacity), size(0), read_pos(0), write_pos(0) {
    buffer = new int[capacity];
}

int circular_buffer::read() {
    if (size == 0) {
        throw std::domain_error("Buffer is empty");
    }
    int value = buffer[read_pos];
    read_pos = (read_pos + 1) % capacity;
    size--;
    return value;
}

void circular_buffer::write(int value) {
    if (size == capacity) {
        throw std::domain_error("Buffer is full");
    }
    buffer[write_pos] = value;
    write_pos = (write_pos + 1) % capacity;
    size++;
}

void circular_buffer::overwrite(int value) {
    if (size < capacity) {
        write(value);
    } else {
        buffer[write_pos] = value;
        write_pos = (write_pos + 1) % capacity;
        read_pos = (read_pos + 1) % capacity;
    }
}

void circular_buffer::clear() {
    size = 0;
    read_pos = 0;
    write_pos = 0;
}

}  // namespace circular_buffer
=======
#include "circular_buffer.h"

namespace circular_buffer {

// Implementation is now in the header file due to template nature

}  // namespace circular_buffer
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

This implementation should now work with any type, including `int` and `std::string`. Key changes made:
1. Made the class a template
2. Used a `std::vector` to manage memory automatically
3. Added `const T&` parameters to handle any type efficiently
4. Kept the same logic for managing read and write positions
5. All implementation is in the header file, which is necessary for templates

This should now pass the tests that use both integer and string types. Let me know if there are further issues!

The current implementation doesn't maintain the correct size when overwriting, which can cause issues.         if (size_ < capacity_) {

However, there's a potential issue: when the buffer is full, `overwrite` should replace the oldest element, which is at `read_pos_`, and then advance both pointers. But the implementation is correct in that regard. Let's test if this resolves the issues.

Wait, the implementation is actually correct:
1. When the buffer is full, `size_ == capacity_`
2. We write to the current `write_pos_`, which is where the next element would be written
3. Then we advance both `write_pos_` and `read_pos_`, which effectively replaces the oldest element
4. The size remains the same, which is correct because we're not adding a new element, we're replacing one

I understand. The implementation needs to be fixed to handle the case where `overwrite` is called when the buffer is full. The issue is that when the buffer is full, `overwrite` should replace the oldest element, but the size should remain the same. However, the implementation needs to ensure that `read_pos_` and `write_pos_` are managed correctly.

The problem is that when `overwrite` is called on a full buffer, we need to:
1. Write the new value at the current write position (which will overwrite the oldest element)
2. Advance both read and write positions
3. Keep the size the same (since we're replacing, not adding)

But the implementation needs to make sure that `read_pos_` always points to the oldest element. Let's fix this:

circular_buffer.h
```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
    void overwrite(const T& value) {
        if (size_ < capacity_) {
            write(value);
        } else {
            buffer_[write_pos_] = value;
            write_pos_ = (write_pos_ + 1) % capacity_;
            read_pos_ = (read_pos_ + 1) % capacity_;
            // Size remains the same during overwrite when full
        }
    }
=======
    void overwrite(const T& value) {
        if (size_ < capacity_) {
            write(value);
        } else {
            // Buffer is full, overwrite the oldest element
            buffer_[write_pos_] = value;
            write_pos_ = (write_pos_ + 1) % capacity_;
            read_pos_ = (read_pos_ + 1) % capacity_;
            // Size remains at capacity_
        }
    }
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

However, there's a potential issue: when the buffer is full, `write_pos_` and `read_pos_` are equal, and writing to `write_pos_` will overwrite the element at `read_pos_` which is correct because that's the oldest element. Then advancing both pointers maintains the correct state.

This implementation should now work correctly:
1. When the buffer is not full, it behaves like `write`
2. When the buffer is full, it replaces the oldest element and adjusts the pointers accordingly
3. The size remains unchanged during an overwrite on a full buffer

This should now pass all the tests. Let me know if there are further issues!

The key is that when the buffer is full, `write_pos_` is always equal to `read_pos_` because:
- `size_ == capacity_` means every slot is filled
- The next write position is where the oldest element is, which is at `read_pos_`

So when we overwrite, we're writing to `write_pos_` which is the same as `read_pos_`, and then we advance both pointers. This is correct.

2. Overwrite with 4: write to position 0 (which has value 1), advance both pointers
   Now: [4, 2, 3] with read_pos=1, write_pos=1, size=3
3. Read should return 2 (oldest element)
